< review>
Appointments, ETA, and other comments/questions were easy over text! Staff was very friendly. My dishwasher and washer weren't draining. The dishwasher fix was quick and easy - works great now. They often had same-day availability to get your appliances working quicker. Washer repair took 3 visits, but a part needed to be ordered and they needed to return for that. I appreciated the 3rd visit as clothing somehow got stuck again right after the 2nd visit for the washer and it made the machine error out again. The 3rd visit didn't require any additional fee. Their labor and parts warranties are for 90 days. The initial review is $65 and if you proceed to have something fixed, it's $185 (65 is applied to 185 if you paid $65 already, otherwise you'll pay $185 total for a fix). However, if parts are required for something, then you'll have to pay for the parts on top of that.

Repair technicians were friendly, professional, and seemed knowledgeable. At times, it was hard to understand them - so just speak to the office staff if you have any detailed questions!

I would recommend them and I loved supporting a local business!</review>

<Rate>4< /Rate>< Text>
Was introduced to this to this spot via take out at a friend's house and it's pretty good. You could have the mala-bowl ("dry") or the mala-tang (soup). Mild is the best with good kick in the flavor especially if you can't hang with spicy food like me. Original is a bit bland but you could always spice it up to your liking. With the mild spicy level, I feel like my tongue gets a little numb and tingly. Then water tastes a little funky, but I chill for a bit and then continue to eat s'mores.

There is a minimum amount items of items you must add to each individual bowl, which is FOUR. You could also double up on some items too if you like. For me, I order the mala-bowl with fish balls with roe, napa cabbage and doubled up on the fishcakes! To maximize our bowls, my boyfriend and I add our own ramen/udon/vermicelli at home. Worth the drive for us because we can't get it all the time.<//Text>

< review>
I was here for lunch and as a first time customer and having been raised in Iowa, I had to learn a little. The menu is how your order is taken.  I asked the waitress about a couple selectable items and she did her best to explain them, but I only had 30min for lunch. I made four selections to compose my bowl and medium spice level. The first taste was delicious! The spice level was perfect between making me sweat and having flavor. The savory side was also perfect. The bowl didn't lack salt and also didn't taste overly salted.  I did try one of the condiments from the three bowls available on the table. I believe the other two are soy sauce and chili oil. The one I tried looked like a miso paste but also had a numbing effect.  I found it delicious but also impeded the taste of the bowl due to the numbing sensation.

I'm excited to go back which leads to my only criticisms.  The hours are a little odd with a closing between 2:30pm and 5pm. It would also be appreciated to have lunch specials or chef suggestions for those of us that are more familiar with a Waffle House or a Cracker Barrel menu.< /review>

< review>
This is a place where you want simple food but yet not so simple, because you have to pick the toppings and noodles, it will take you some time to make up your mind what you want to eat (if you have the so-called 選擇困難症）but the food is delicious there! I chose lamb, bok choy, oysters mushrooms, tofu skins, octopus balls and vermicelli, with a mild spicy soup. All the ingredients tasted good and I feel like I am having my own hotpot. One thing I hope is that they don’t make the soup base so salty. But you can order a bowl of rice on the side I think that would help to wash down the saltiness.</review>

<Rating>5< /Rating>< Text>
Got coffee, bagels and sandwiches?
Cassidy’s Corner Cafe in Bixby Knolls, California is the spot to go. They're serving up freshly baked bagels, coffee and delicious sandwiches daily. What keeps me coming back to Cassidy’s Corner Cafe - Bixby Knolls? It's the quality of the food and service that keeps me coming back for more. I've been a loyal customer since their grand opening in July of 2020. Cassidy’s is located at 3846 Atlantic Avenue in Long Beach, California. The bagel shop is open 7 days a week from 6:00 am - 2:00 pm. No indoor dining yet but they have a nice outdoor patio in the front of the shop. Come early because some of the specialty bagels sell out quick.

I ordered the Cassidy’s Club sandwich along with their Signature 4-2-1 Ice Coffee yesterday. Today, I'm having another delicious Cassidy’s Club sandwich with their sweet Thai Ice Tea. My sandwiches came with turkey, crispy bacon, avocado, tomatoes, red onions, lettuce and dijon mustard with my choice of an Asiago bagel. I love the fact that Cassidy’s uses quality Boar's Head Premium product for their sandwiches. Using quality ingredients is always a recipe for success. Today, my club sandwich came with my favorite quote " You can be anywhere in the world...and you chose Cassidy’s." It's the personal touch, paired with quality food and service that will keep customers like myself coming back for more. Drop by for breakfast or lunch if you've in the neighborhood. Tell them Kev Pai recommended you here to for the best bagels and sandwiches in town.< /Text>

< Text>
I've been coming here for a couple months now. They have the most delicious and amazing breakfast bagels. Personally love The Desy. Their bagels are always fresh and unfortunately that can also be a downer because they run out after a while. The location itself is OK. They have street parking in the front. In the mornings it isn't too full and usually they have parking. I do not know about the afternoons though. The staff is great. Everyone is nice and patient. They take both online and phone orders. < name>
Kymberlyn Reed</name>
<Text>I've loved the Kinokuniya bookstore in Little Tokyo for years. This was my first foray to this one and I love it just as much. FYI: it's located inside the Mitsuwa Marketplace, so when you see that, you're headed in the right direction. I'm a pen junkie, and Kinokuniya has everything I could ever want. I've learned that the Japanese really love their writing implements and are great at developing all types of pens for optimum writing experience. Of course there's manga aplenty, along with tons of awesome blank books, journals, stationery, plushies, cute tote bags (check out the Gojira/Godzilla one). The sales staff are really friendly too. Definitely worth a second and third trip. Plus, right next door is a market specializing in all Japanese food and sundry items, including fresh sushi to go, as well as shops with all manner of Japanese fast food. Shop then eat. Sounds like a plan.<//Text><Gmap_id>0x80c2ba5c01c87edd:0x9b7c23a17bb32289<//Gmap_id><Date>1502420104184</Date>< Rating>

<response>None</response>< review>
Don't do it! First of all, it's 102 today and inside is 88. It's ridiculous. The car wash options have 3 basic tiers with the most expensive at $21.99, plus add on options. I'm not sure how the wash itself will turn out, but it really doesn't matter. No paying customer should ever be this uncomfortable. When you walk into the "retail" section, you'll see LOTS of empty space, as they lack the products that decent car washes offer. They have a few cold beverages, some chips, and about 6 air fresheners to choose from. In the waiting area, there are two non working televisions above a filthy counter top, and one that does work that's set to a current legal trial. There's also a clock that displays the wrong time by about 2 hours. Save yourself the anxiety and don't waste your time or money here.

Update: After leaving this awful place, I found trash that they left in my car. Rather than using traditional air fresheners (they ask what scent you'd like when you arrive), they throw little pieces of paper soaked in liquid all over the car. I found them under all of my seats and between the console and the seats. Disgusting. I imagine these can probably damage carpets and upholstery as well.<//review>

< review>
Historic open air place where many hollywood stars made their impressions of their hands and shoe prints on cement. In front of Graumanns Chinese Theatre, this is a MUST place to go in LA where you will see many imprints of your favorite past and present celebrities.</review>

A sacred place for movies and what accomplishments have taken them to.
I loved this place, filled with so many memories of movies and people who have made an impact on my life.
You can put your hands and feet on the ground where other actors have been, and compare them to your own.
The only problem here was, like the same street, it's filled with people who aboard you all the time, and don't let you enjoy the moment to yourself.
My favorite place in Hollywood, definitely!< /Text>

< review>
A sacred place for movies and what accomplishments have taken them to.
I loved this place, filled with so many memories of movies and people who have made an impact on my life.
You can put your hands and feet on the ground where other actors have been, and compare them to your own.
The only problem here was, like the same street, it's filled with people who aboard you all the time, and don't let you enjoy the moment to yourself.
My favorite place in Hollywood, definitely!< /review>
